  <div class="mw-parser-output">
   <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
    Hierarchy of complexity classes for formulas defining sets
   </div> 
   <div class="thumb tright">
    <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;">
     <a href="/wiki/File:Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg/302px-Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg.png" decoding="async" width="302" height="513" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg/453px-Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg/604px-Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="335" data-file-height="569"></a> 
     <div class="thumbcaption">
      <div class="magnify">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Arithmetic_hierarchy.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
      </div>An illustration of how the levels of the hierarchy interact and where some basic set categories lie within it.
     </div>
    </div>
   </div> 
   <p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_logic" title="Mathematical logic">mathematical logic</a>, the <b>arithmetical hierarchy</b>, <b>arithmetic hierarchy</b> or <b><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Cole_Kleene" title="Stephen Cole Kleene">Kleene</a>–<a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Mostowski" title="Andrzej Mostowski">Mostowski</a> hierarchy</b> classifies certain <a href="/wiki/Set_(mathematics)" title="Set (mathematics)">sets</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Complexity" title="Complexity">complexity</a> of formulas that define them. Any set that receives a classification is called <b>arithmetical</b>. </p>
   <p>The arithmetical hierarchy is important in <a href="/wiki/Recursion_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Recursion theory">recursion theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Effective_descriptive_set_theory" title="Effective descriptive set theory">effective descriptive set theory</a>, and the study of formal theories such as <a href="/wiki/Peano_arithmetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Peano arithmetic">Peano arithmetic</a>. </p>
   <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tarski%E2%80%93Kuratowski_algorithm" title="Tarski–Kuratowski algorithm">Tarski–Kuratowski algorithm</a> provides an easy way to get an upper bound on the classifications assigned to a formula and the set it defines. </p>
   <p>The <a href="/wiki/Hyperarithmetical_hierarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperarithmetical hierarchy">hyperarithmetical hierarchy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Analytical_hierarchy" title="Analytical hierarchy">analytical hierarchy</a> extend the arithmetical hierarchy to classify additional formulas and sets. </p> 
   <div id="toc" class="toc">

   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arithmetical_hierarchy_of_formulas">The arithmetical hierarchy of formulas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: The arithmetical hierarchy of formulas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>The arithmetical hierarchy assigns classifications to the formulas in the language of <a href="/wiki/Peano_axioms#First-order_theory_of_arithmetic" title="Peano axioms">first-order arithmetic</a>. The classifications are denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}">

           <mi mathvariant="normal">

            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7a4ef07c43c84a667249d8d7400a79d53b0c1577" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.897ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Sigma _{n}^{0}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}">

            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

The Greek letters here are <a href="/wiki/Lightface" class="mw-redirect" title="Lightface">lightface</a> symbols, which indicates that the formulas do not contain set parameters. </p>

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle n-1}">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}">

   <p>Because every formula is equivalent to a formula in <a href="/wiki/Prenex_normal_form" title="Prenex normal form">prenex normal form</a>, every formula with no set quantifiers is assigned at least one classification. Because redundant quantifiers can be added to any formula, once a formula is assigned the classification <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7a4ef07c43c84a667249d8d7400a79d53b0c1577" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.897ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Sigma _{n}^{0}"></span> or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow>

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{m}^{0}}">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{m}^{0}}">

         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->

           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

             m
            </mi>

The most important classification assigned to a formula is thus the one with the least <i>n</i>, because this is enough to determine all the other classifications. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arithmetical_hierarchy_of_sets_of_natural_numbers">The arithmetical hierarchy of sets of natural numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The arithmetical hierarchy of sets of natural numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>A set <i>X</i> of natural numbers is defined by formula φ in the language of <a href="/wiki/Peano_arithmetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Peano arithmetic">Peano arithmetic</a> (the first-order language with symbols "0" for zero, "S" for the successor function, "+" for addition, "×" for multiplication, and "=" for equality), if the elements of <i>X</i> are exactly the numbers that satisfy φ. That is, for all natural numbers <i>n</i>, </p> 
   <dl>
    <dd>
     <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle n\in X\Leftrightarrow \mathbb {N} \models \varphi ({\underline {n}}),}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <mi>
            n
           </mi> 
           <mo>
            ∈
            <!-- ∈ -->
           </mo> 
           <mi>
            X
           </mi> 
           <mo stretchy="false">
            ⇔
            <!-- ⇔ -->
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi mathvariant="double-struck">
             N
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mo>
            ⊨
            <!-- ⊨ -->
           </mo> 
           <mi>
            φ
            <!-- φ -->
           </mi> 
           <mo stretchy="false">
            (
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <munder> 
             <mi>
              n
             </mi> 
             <mo>
              _
              <!-- _ -->
             </mo> 
            </munder> 
           </mrow> 
           <mo stretchy="false">
            )
           </mo> 
           <mo>
            ,
           </mo> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle n\in X\Leftrightarrow \mathbb {N} \models \varphi ({\underline {n}}),}
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2d207bc1736ddea42b7e5e611e8bcc6b1f13c7cd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.583ex; margin-bottom: -0.755ex; width:20.186ex; height:3.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle n\in X\Leftrightarrow \mathbb {N} \models \varphi ({\underline {n}}),}"></span>
    </dd>
   </dl> 
   <p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle {\underline {n}}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
           <munder> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
            <mo>
             _
             <!-- _ -->
            </mo> 
           </munder> 
          </mrow> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle {\underline {n}}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/108cd33672c17a80b82fbc171483f7e6d5b7fd5b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.537ex; margin-bottom: -0.801ex; width:1.397ex; height:2.676ex;" alt="\underline n"></span> is the numeral in the language of arithmetic corresponding to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle n}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           n
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle n}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="n"></span>. A set is definable in first-order arithmetic if it is defined by some formula in the language of Peano arithmetic. </p>
   <p>Each set <i>X</i> of natural numbers that is definable in first-order arithmetic is assigned classifications of the form <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}">

            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7a4ef07c43c84a667249d8d7400a79d53b0c1577" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.897ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Sigma _{n}^{0}"></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dff818a17097e6a635c1fba3291945703e60825a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^0_n"></span>, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Δ
            <!-- Δ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

           </mrow>

        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Delta _{n}^{0}}

   <p>A parallel definition is used to define the arithmetical hierarchy on finite <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartesian power">Cartesian powers</a> of the set of natural numbers. Instead of formulas with one free variable, formulas with <i>k</i> free number variables are used to define the arithmetical hierarchy on sets of <i>k</i>-<a href="/wiki/Tuple" title="Tuple">tuples</a> of natural numbers. These are in fact related by the use of a <a href="/wiki/Pairing_function" title="Pairing function">pairing function</a>. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relativized_arithmetical_hierarchies">Relativized arithmetical hierarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Relativized arithmetical hierarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>Just as we can define what it means for a set <i>X</i> to be <a href="/wiki/Recursive_set" title="Recursive set">recursive</a> relative to another set <i>Y</i> by allowing the computation defining <i>X</i> to consult <i>Y</i> as an oracle we can extend this notion to the whole arithmetic hierarchy and define what it means for <i>X</i> to be <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}

      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f1f827c279a8cb7e635d2caf95f9a1d8be76bd3c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.701ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Delta^{0,Y}_n"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>

            <mo>

            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cf87feddc8b7c7d1cd116920f7221923b3e696f7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.509ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Pi^{0,Y}_n"></span>. To do so, fix a set of integers <i>Y</i> and add a predicate for membership in <i>Y</i> to the language of Peano arithmetic. We then say that <i>X</i> is in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}">

           </mi>

             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow>

             0
            </mn> 
            <mo>
             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f78c8bae525183cfa2318c732b5588f8f2942ef" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.444ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma^{0,Y}_n"></span> if it is defined by a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow>

         </mstyle>

        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics>

In other words, <i>X</i> is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}">

            <mn>

            </mn>

             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f78c8bae525183cfa2318c732b5588f8f2942ef" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.444ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma^{0,Y}_n"></span> if it is defined by a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}">

Alternatively one can view the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics>

           </mi>

            </mn>

            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi>

          </msubsup>

        </mrow>

         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation>

   <p>For example, let <i>Y</i> be a set of integers. Let <i>X</i> be the set of numbers divisible by an element of Y. Then <i>X</i> is defined by the formula <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics>

         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{0}^{0,Y}}">

   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arithmetic_reducibility_and_degrees">Arithmetic reducibility and degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Arithmetic reducibility and degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>Arithmetical reducibility is an intermediate notion between <a href="/wiki/Turing_reducibility" class="mw-redirect" title="Turing reducibility">Turing reducibility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyperarithmetic_reducibility" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperarithmetic reducibility">hyperarithmetic reducibility</a>. </p>
   <p>A set is <b>arithmetical</b> (also <b>arithmetic</b> and <b>arithmetically definable</b>) if it is defined by some formula in the language of Peano arithmetic. Equivalently <i>X</i> is arithmetical if <i>X</i> is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7a4ef07c43c84a667249d8d7400a79d53b0c1577" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.897ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Sigma _{n}^{0}"></span> or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dff818a17097e6a635c1fba3291945703e60825a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^0_n"></span> for some integer <i>n</i>. A set <i>X</i> <b>is arithmetical in</b> a set <i>Y</i>, denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           X
          </mi> 
          <msub> 
           <mo>
            ≤
            <!-- ≤ -->
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             A
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msub> 
          <mi>
           Y
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c30b84fb7b2a3b81a7282a430fa66a9ac19b3bac" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.317ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="X \leq_A Y"></span>, if <i>X</i> is definable a some formula in the language of Peano arithmetic extended by a predicate for membership in <i>Y</i>. Equivalently, <i>X</i> is arithmetical in <i>Y</i> if <i>X</i> is in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
            <mo>
             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f78c8bae525183cfa2318c732b5588f8f2942ef" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.444ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma^{0,Y}_n"></span> or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
            <mo>
             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cf87feddc8b7c7d1cd116920f7221923b3e696f7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.509ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Pi^{0,Y}_n"></span> for some integer <i>n</i>. A synonym for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           X
          </mi> 
          <msub> 
           <mo>
            ≤
            <!-- ≤ -->
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             A
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msub> 
          <mi>
           Y
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c30b84fb7b2a3b81a7282a430fa66a9ac19b3bac" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.317ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="X \leq_A Y"></span> is: <i>X</i> is <b>arithmetically reducible</b> to <i>Y</i>. </p>
   <p>The relation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           X
          </mi> 
          <msub> 
           <mo>
            ≤
            <!-- ≤ -->
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             A
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msub> 
          <mi>
           Y
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle X\leq _{A}Y}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c30b84fb7b2a3b81a7282a430fa66a9ac19b3bac" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.317ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="X \leq_A Y"></span> is reflexive and transitive, and thus the relation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \equiv _{A}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msub>

           </mo>

   <dl>
    <dd>
     <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

    </dd>

   <p>is an equivalence relation. The equivalence classes of this relation are called the <b>arithmetic degrees</b>; they are partially ordered under <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \leq _{A}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msub>

            <!-- ≤ -->
           </mo> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             A
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msub> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \leq _{A}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6b0455bd184718baf034523bb7e7d91ede33ceef" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.273ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="\leq_A"></span>. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arithmetical_hierarchy_of_subsets_of_Cantor_and_Baire_space">The arithmetical hierarchy of subsets of Cantor and Baire space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The arithmetical hierarchy of subsets of Cantor and Baire space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cantor_space" title="Cantor space">Cantor space</a>, denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle 2^{\omega }}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msup> 
           <mn>
            2
           </mn> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             ω
             <!-- ω -->
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle 2^{\omega }}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86c530fc66607b5c5d565bf2e4a0ccf64382c6e2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.417ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="2^{\omega}"></span>, is the set of all infinite sequences of 0s and 1s; the <a href="/wiki/Baire_space_(set_theory)" title="Baire space (set theory)">Baire space</a>, denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \omega ^{\omega }}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msup> 
           <mi>
            ω
            <!-- ω -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             ω
             <!-- ω -->
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \omega ^{\omega }}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9aa5636cabcea62c44c8b91fd9095e06054a6fa4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.7ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="\omega^{\omega}"></span> or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi class="MJX-tex-caligraphic" mathvariant="script">
             N
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </mrow> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7551c7bed2cd2ee83e10536d157c94a5f8f72fd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-left: -0.062ex; width:2.337ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\mathcal {N}}"></span>, is the set of all infinite sequences of natural numbers. Note that elements of the Cantor space can be identified with sets of integers and elements of the Baire space with functions from integers to integers. </p>
   <p>The ordinary axiomatization of <a href="/wiki/Second-order_arithmetic" title="Second-order arithmetic">second-order arithmetic</a> uses a set-based language in which the set quantifiers can naturally be viewed as quantifying over Cantor space. A subset of Cantor space is assigned the classification <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

   <p>Note that while both the elements of the Cantor space (regarded as sets of integers) and subsets of the Cantor space are classified in arithmetic hierarchies, these are not the same hierarchy. In fact the relationship between the two hierarchies is interesting and non-trivial. For instance the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dff818a17097e6a635c1fba3291945703e60825a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^0_n"></span> elements of the Cantor space are not (in general) the same as the elements <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>

          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow>

         {\displaystyle X}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="X"></span> of the Cantor space so that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \{X\}}">

        </annotation>

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi>

            </mn> 
           </mrow>

         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dff818a17097e6a635c1fba3291945703e60825a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^0_n"></span> subset of the Cantor space. However, many interesting results relate the two hierarchies. </p>
   <p>There are two ways that a subset of Baire space can be classified in the arithmetical hierarchy. </p> 
   <ul>
    <li>A subset of Baire space has a corresponding subset of Cantor space under the map that takes each function from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \omega }"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <mi>
            ω
            <!-- ω -->
           </mi> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle \omega }
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48eff443f9de7a985bb94ca3bde20813ea737be8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.446ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="\omega "></span> to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \omega }"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <mi>
            ω
            <!-- ω -->
           </mi> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle \omega }
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48eff443f9de7a985bb94ca3bde20813ea737be8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.446ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="\omega "></span> to the <a href="/wiki/Indicator_function" title="Indicator function">characteristic function</a> of its graph. A subset of Baire space is given the classification <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{1}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

            </mi>

       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{1}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

            </mi>

             </mi> 
            </mrow> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
             <mn>
              1
             </mn> 
            </mrow> 
           </msubsup> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{1}}
         </annotation>

       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0425229e269e018ad344ea86ab55bd540ceb0e9a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^1_n"></span>, or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

    <li>An equivalent definition of the analytical hierarchy on Baire space is given by defining the analytical hierarchy of formulas using a functional version of second-order arithmetic; then the analytical hierarchy on subsets of Cantor space can be defined from the hierarchy on Baire space. This alternate definition gives exactly the same classifications as the first definition.</li>
   </ul> 
   <p>A parallel definition is used to define the arithmetical hierarchy on finite Cartesian powers of Baire space or Cantor space, using formulas with several free variables. The arithmetical hierarchy can be defined on any <a href="/wiki/Effective_Polish_space" title="Effective Polish space">effective Polish space</a>; the definition is particularly simple for Cantor space and Baire space because they fit with the language of ordinary second-order arithmetic. </p>
   <p>Note that we can also define the arithmetic hierarchy of subsets of the Cantor and Baire spaces relative to some set of integers. In fact boldface <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {\Sigma } _{n}^{0}}">

        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup>

             <!-- Σ -->
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \mathbf {\Sigma } _{n}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a506c9138e33267ba07756c2270d7a61356bbf54" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.15ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \mathbf {\Sigma } _{n}^{0}}"></span> is just the union of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>

            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

            </mo>

Note that the boldface hierarchy is just the standard hierarchy of <a href="/wiki/Borel_hierarchy" title="Borel hierarchy">Borel sets</a>. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extensions_and_variations">Extensions and variations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Extensions and variations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>It is possible to define the arithmetical hierarchy of formulas using a language extended with a function symbol for each <a href="/wiki/Primitive_recursive_function" title="Primitive recursive function">primitive recursive function</a>. This variation slightly changes the classification of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

   <p>A more semantic variation of the hierarchy can be defined on all finitary relations on the natural numbers; the following definition is used. Every computable relation is defined to be <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

The classifications <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}">

It can be extended to cover finitary relations on the natural numbers, Baire space, and Cantor space. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meaning_of_the_notation">Meaning of the notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Meaning of the notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>The following meanings can be attached to the notation for the arithmetical hierarchy on formulas. </p>
   <p>The subscript <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle n}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           n
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle n}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="n"></span> in the symbols <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

   <p>The superscript <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle 0}">

      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2aae8864a3c1fec9585261791a809ddec1489950" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.162ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle 0}"></span> in the symbols <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}">

      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{n}^{0}}">

      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/333e776b9cc01a4531d07e0c785533b45b7ce04b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.154ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Delta _{n}^{0}"></span> indicates the type of the objects being quantified over. Type 0 objects are natural numbers, and objects of type <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle i+1}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           i
          </mi> 
          <mo>
           +
          </mo> 
          <mn>
           1
          </mn> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle i+1}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2fe1bfc8314922e4c3fdb4e8eceb20a00b4f011d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:4.805ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="i+1"></span> are functions that map the set of objects of type <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle i}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <mi>
           i
          </mi> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle i}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/add78d8608ad86e54951b8c8bd6c8d8416533d20" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.802ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="i"></span> to the natural numbers. Quantification over higher type objects, such as functions from natural numbers to natural numbers, is described by a superscript greater than 0, as in the <a href="/wiki/Analytical_hierarchy" title="Analytical hierarchy">analytical hierarchy</a>. The superscript 0 indicates quantifiers over numbers, the superscript 1 would indicate quantification over functions from numbers to numbers (type 1 objects), the superscript 2 would correspond to quantification over functions that take a type 1 object and return a number, and so on. </p> 
   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <ul>
    <li>The <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <msubsup>

             Σ
             <!-- Σ -->
            </mi> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
             <mn>
              1
             </mn> 
            </mrow> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
             <mn>

             </mn> 
            </mrow>

          {\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}

         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e2bb8500ed22c81245cfdac7b772b8df05a0a96a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:27.522ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\exists n_1 \cdots \exists n_k \psi(n_1,\ldots,n_k,m)"></span> where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \psi }">

These are exactly the <a href="/wiki/Recursively_enumerable_set" title="Recursively enumerable set">recursively enumerable sets</a>.</li> 
    <li>The set of natural numbers that are indices for Turing machines that compute total functions is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{2}^{0}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

             Π
             <!-- Π -->
            </mi> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              2
             </mn>

             <mn>

             </mn> 
            </mrow>

          </mstyle>

Intuitively, an index <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e}">

       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle m}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          {\displaystyle m}
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="m"></span> "there is an <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle s}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <mi>
            s
           </mi> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle s}
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="s"></span> such that the Turing machine with index <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

          {\displaystyle e}

       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle m}">

          {\displaystyle m}
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="m"></span> after <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle s}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <mi>

           </mi>

         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

         </annotation>

       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="s"></span> steps”. A complete proof would show that the property displayed in quotes in the previous sentence is definable in the language of Peano arithmetic by a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
           <msubsup>

    <li>Every <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}">

Moreover, for any such set there is a computable enumeration of Gödel numbers of basic open sets whose union is the original set. For this reason, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}">

            </mi>

             <mn>

             </mn> 
            </mrow> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
             <mn>
              0
             </mn> 
            </mrow> 
           </msubsup> 
          </mstyle> 
         </mrow>

Similarly, every <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

    <li>Every arithmetical subset of Cantor space or Baire space is a <a href="/wiki/Borel_set" title="Borel set">Borel set</a>. The lightface Borel hierarchy extends the arithmetical hierarchy to include additional Borel sets. For example, every <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

The time for this is polynomial in their arguments (e.g. polynomial in <i>n</i> for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

This no longer holds under alternative definitions of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

            </mi>

   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <p>The following properties hold for the arithmetical hierarchy of sets of natural numbers and the arithmetical hierarchy of subsets of Cantor or Baire space. </p> 
   <ul>
    <li>The collections <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

             <!-- Π -->
            </mi>

              n
             </mi> 
            </mrow> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
             <mn>
              0
             </mn> 
            </mrow>

          </mstyle> 
         </mrow> 
         <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
          {\displaystyle \Pi _{n}^{0}}
         </annotation> 
        </semantics> 
       </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dff818a17097e6a635c1fba3291945703e60825a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.962ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="\Pi^0_n"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
       <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n}^{0}}"> 
        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
          <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

             <!-- Σ -->
            </mi> 
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

    <li>A set is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

   <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relation_to_Turing_machines">Relation to Turing machines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Relation to Turing machines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
   <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
    See also: 
    <a href="/wiki/Post%27s_theorem" title="Post's theorem">Post's theorem</a>
   </div> 
   <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computable_sets">Computable sets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Computable sets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
   <p>If S is a <a href="/wiki/Computable_function#Computable_sets_and_relations" title="Computable function">Turing computable set</a>, then both S and its <a href="/wiki/Complement_(set_theory)" title="Complement (set theory)">complement</a> are recursively enumerable (if T is a Turing machine giving 1 for inputs in S and 0 otherwise, we may build a Turing machine halting only on the former, and another halting only on the latter). </p>
   <p>By <a href="/wiki/Post%27s_theorem" title="Post's theorem">Post's theorem</a>, both S and its complement are in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8130a55f302deb0b733de5a526f2d92c364e4dd6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.732ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma _{1}^{0}"></span>. This means that S is both in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8130a55f302deb0b733de5a526f2d92c364e4dd6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.732ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma _{1}^{0}"></span> and in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Pi _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Π
            <!-- Π -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Pi _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b0b3c0e79d8a5db977a9838be477eb3e30348937" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.797ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Pi _{1}^{0}"></span>, and hence it is in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Δ
            <!-- Δ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/472ac09286b20746e38e3a31a9f4feccbd4a0a23" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.99ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Delta^0_1"></span>. </p>
   <p>Similarly, for every set S in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Δ
            <!-- Δ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/472ac09286b20746e38e3a31a9f4feccbd4a0a23" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.99ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Delta^0_1"></span>, both S and its complement are in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8130a55f302deb0b733de5a526f2d92c364e4dd6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.732ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma _{1}^{0}"></span> and are therefore (by <a href="/wiki/Post%27s_theorem" title="Post's theorem">Post's theorem</a>) recursively enumerable by some Turing machines T<sub>1</sub> and T<sub>2</sub>, respectively. For every number n, exactly one of these halts. We may therefore construct a Turing machine T that alternates between T<sub>1</sub> and T<sub>2</sub>, halting and returning 1 when the former halts or halting and returning 0 when the latter halts. Thus T halts on every n and returns whether it is in S, So S is computable. </p> 
   <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary_of_main_results">Summary of main results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arithmetical_hierarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Summary of main results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
   <p>The Turing computable sets of natural numbers are exactly the sets at level <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Δ
            <!-- Δ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/472ac09286b20746e38e3a31a9f4feccbd4a0a23" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.99ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Delta^0_1"></span> of the arithmetical hierarchy. The recursively enumerable sets are exactly the sets at level <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{1}^{0}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8130a55f302deb0b733de5a526f2d92c364e4dd6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.732ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Sigma _{1}^{0}"></span>. </p>
   <p>No <a href="/wiki/Oracle_machine" title="Oracle machine">oracle machine</a> is capable of solving its own <a href="/wiki/Halting_problem" title="Halting problem">halting problem</a> (a variation of Turing's proof applies). The halting problem for a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{n}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Δ
            <!-- Δ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
            <mo>
             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Delta _{n}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f1f827c279a8cb7e635d2caf95f9a1d8be76bd3c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.701ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="\Delta^{0,Y}_n"></span> oracle in fact sits in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma _{n+1}^{0,Y}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
          <msubsup> 
           <mi mathvariant="normal">
            Σ
            <!-- Σ -->
           </mi> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mi>
             n
            </mi> 
            <mo>
             +
            </mo> 
            <mn>
             1
            </mn> 
           </mrow> 
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
            <mn>
             0
            </mn> 
            <mo>
             ,
            </mo> 
            <mi>
             Y
            </mi> 
           </mrow> 
          </msubsup> 
         </mstyle> 
        </mrow> 
        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
         {\displaystyle \Sigma _{n+1}^{0,Y}}
        </annotation> 
       </semantics> 
      </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0af7a2e255a8aed2fc295be5c1837be63b9a4956" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:4.997ex; height:3.676ex;" alt="\Sigma^{0,Y}_{n+1}"></span>. </p>
   <p><a href="/wiki/Post%27s_theorem" title="Post's theorem">Post's theorem</a> establishes a close connection between the arithmetical hierarchy of sets of natural numbers and the <a href="/wiki/Turing_degree" title="Turing degree">Turing degrees</a>. In particular, it establishes the following facts for all <i>n</i> ≥ 1: </p> 
   <ul>
    <li>The set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        <semantics> 
         <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

             <!-- ∅ -->
            </mi>

             </mo>

             </mi>

             </mn> 
            </mrow> 
           </msubsup> 
          </mstyle>

   </ul> 
   <p>The <a href="/wiki/Polynomial_hierarchy" title="Polynomial hierarchy">polynomial hierarchy</a> is a "feasible resource-bounded" version of the arithmetical hierarchy in which polynomial length bounds are placed on the numbers involved (or, equivalently, polynomial time bounds are placed on the Turing machines involved). It gives a finer classification of some sets of natural numbers that are at level <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
      <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{1}^{0}}"> 
       <semantics> 
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
         <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
